<review>We love our neighborhood, but we, too, are experiencing serious issues with getting our USPS mail delivered to us.

We've had problems with sending personal letters, greeting cards (which we confirmed didn't make it) and checks (that we had to cancel) from the outside boxes at the USPS-MV branch. We talked to them and they responded in a tone as if that was common knowledge that "yeah, those boxes get broken into frequently, you should never use those" (!).

We've had several packages stolen (they claim they were delivered and marked them as such, anyway) while we were home awaiting deliveries (no one ever knocks and we have no windows facing in a way that we could see them walking up to our door), as well as several incoming pay checks missing from our mail, with no evidence of a broken mailbox.

When it comes to deliveries, they often leave packages sitting anywhere from on the ground in the general area of our mailbox (close to the sidewalk/curb) to the other end of the property by the alleyway and several times they have literally thrown (!) packages up our one full flight of stairs. Last time it happened, I was only a couple of seconds away from the front door and I heard it happen, so I peeked out and the face of the lady "delivering" the package revealed that she was shocked to see me, as she was more or less running away from me. It looked as funny as it sounds...

We make sure to always have someone be home when a package is to be delivered, especially since we've had several packages gone missing, and we also closely follow tracking details (USPS tracking details are especially off at the MV branch, as they randomly seem to mark packages delivered before they even start their route and other times retrospectively at the end of the day), yet they have not even one single time knocked on our door.

At the post office, we've repeatedly talked to the post master and he basically says there's nothing he can or will do and that we should probably make sure anything important and especially all pay checks are sent to us insured and with tracking numbers added. We were shocked to hear him say that. My partner replied out loud what I was thinking too: "you're basically saying that to actually get your mail delivered, you have to pay extra and get tracking and insurance?". His response was to tell my partner that being sarcastic wasn't helping (!). Problem is he wasn't being sarcastic, there's nothing funny about any of it. Even if we wanted to do what he told us, we are both freelancers with varying people and companies sending us checks from places we don't always know (3rd parties are often involved), and therefore it is not a possibility for us.

Over the past two years, we've also done probably a dozen mail holds and we always make sure to add one extra day in case we're delayed coming home. Turns out every single time we've done a mail hold in the past at this local post office, they have delivered our mail anyway, including their own note to hold our mail (!). It doesn't matter if we do the hold request online or in person (as they suggested after our first few complaints).

The only exception was the last time when we did the option of picking up our mail in person and we came in a day early and they simply didn't have it, telling us it was because it was "probably out with the carrier" (!). When we went back the next day and finally got our mail, it contained another person's mail as well (unfortunately that's not unusual, not just previous residents', but neighbors' at other addresses) that looked very important and urgent and had been sitting in our hold for a week. We saw it before we left there and immediately informed them of that and they asked if we were really sure we didn't know this person? (!)... Thinking of all the possible letters of our own that we don't even know that we've been missing out on over the years makes me quite mad.

I'm not joking when I say we have considering moving because of the local post office.</review>< Pictures>

< Review>
A fun and welcoming studio for recreational choreography, and fitness dance classes.  the instructors are mostly fun and upbeat and lead great single classes.  This isn't too much of a technical learning studio, more of a place for people who love to dance to come and take classes where they can learn choreo to current songs in an hour.  There are lots of different hip hops as well as some west African/Latin fusion/burlesque style classes. Also plenty of fitness dance classes like Zumba and groove.<//Review>

< text>
I live in a two bedroom apartment here and the living room is a good size for one large couch as well as a small couch. Also, the living room can fit a small dinner table. The kitchen that my roommates and I have fit a refrigerator, a sink, dishwasher, and a gas oven/ stove. There are plenty of cabinets in the kitchen, all three of us are able to store and fit our own kitchen wear and food. the kitchen is connected to a hallway. the guest bathroom is a god size with tub and shower. The master bedroom is a good size that can fit two twin size beds. The closet is big too, but the sliding door can be hard to open. The master bed room's bathroom has the sink separated from the shower and toilet. the counter space is roomy. My only complaints about Campus Crossing is that there are few parking spaces in the front. Of course I have my own parking spot, but I prefer parking in the front. Also, the apartments are not closed off from the streets, so make sure that at night the front door apartment's are well secure and closed. I find the maintenance here pretty good, but that could be because this is my first apartment. Also, the apartment staff provide little events every month and they can range from free food to crafts to movie night. If you are a student at UCR, its pretty close to the school and easy walking distance. If you don't feel like walking there is a bus that can easily take you to the front of UCR.</text>

<Pics>None< /Pics>< Review>
To summarize my experience here, you pretty much get what you pay for (maybe less) compared to other apartments near the UCR campus in terms of quality.

Campus Crossings is one of the very few apartment complexes that allows you to sign a 10-month lease plan, which is one of the major reasons why my friends and I chose to stay here. In addition, the price was relatively low compared to the other places we looked at. The customer service is also very nice and will help you with your troubles.

Upon moving in, our 3 bedroom 2 bathroom unit was clean overall. There were, however, some weird "adjustments/fixes" made, such as a giant patch in the carpet because of a previous stain and the floor near one of the bedrooms not being level, but these aren't major issues.

Throughout the year, there have been a lot of water maintenances and shutoffs. However, these occur most of the time when I am at school, so it hasn't affected me all that much. Speaking of water, the temperature of the water tends to fluctuate a lot, which is a bit annoying.

We haven't really experienced any roach or bug problems, but this is most likely because we live on the 2nd floor. Although, there have been a lot of dead bees that end up on our porch.

One of my main complaints with the apartment is how it was advertised as "gated", because this place is NOT gated. Anyone can literally walk into the complex, so there have been several times when I've encountered homeless people digging through the trash while I was throwing out my own. In addition, because of the amount of homeless people, I've experienced my bike being messed with (including my back wheel coming close to falling off and the chains being touched). The only reason I lock it outside is because we don't have room to put it in the apartment. Therefore, I strongly think they should take off the "gated" feature off the website to prevent people from thinking this place is actually gated (I also didn't get to check out the apartment before moving in because I am from NorCal and signed the lease over the summer online).

I'd say that if you are in your "last resort" phase in looking for a place to stay for the school year, then come here. Other than that, I'd rather pay a bit more for somewhere that is higher in quality.</Review>

You wrote a review for Pizza Hut	3 weeks ago
1.0 star rating7/5/2020
This was a 1st time order from this location.

DELIVERY ORDER: Large 2 topping, thin crust pizza, 12pc hot wings.
COST (without driver tip): $36.79

I have consumed quite a few pizza slices in my life for literally, decades. Having my first ever as a child at Shakey's in San Gabriel, I was hooked!

This pizza was THE ABSOLUTE WORST I have ever experienced. Two others who shared it also agreed. If, as a child I had experienced this pizza as my first, I would have an aversion to pizza and everyone would think I was weird.

Moral of the story:  Don't assume that because you had a good Pizza Hut pizza in the past somewhere that you'll  get that same quality at another location...<//text>

I would have ordered online to use coupons, but there system was down, and the price came to be 36.00$ + tax. I was fine paying this absurd price, but the problem occured when the pizza arrived. The pizza was nothing but grease, pooling in the middle of the pizza. I tried ignoring it, tried padding it with a napkin, but it was simply too much. My stomach began to ache from all of the grease of the pizza. The cookie, was not even sliced as it usually always is, and was just baked and tossed into the box. Highly disappointed and incredibly dissatisfied. Waste of my money. This is the first time this Pizza Hut has reached this level of low for me. Cheers.</review>

<Name>Shan Serran< /Name><pictures>None< /pictures>< text>
We ordered their New York Special and Shrimp Pesto medium size pizzas. Overall, both we're pretty good. The crust is thin and they throughly spread the toppings and cheese to the very end of the crust. Unlike some places where the crust is thick and lots of crust. Because the crust is thin, your slice of pizza does tend to get limp which is not bad when it's hot and fresh. I recommend giving them a try and take advantage of their website coupons. Their online ordering system is also very easier to use so check that out too. I'll go there again and probably try their other pizzas.</text>

<review>I don't give five stars lightly.

This place is worth the 20 minute drive from Buttonwillow/I-5 if you have the time.

Was here for breakfast. It is NOT fast food. It was cooked to order and took a few extra minutes. Worth the wait.

I particularly enjoyed the biscuits & gravy. The omelette was pretty good. Not the best I've ever had, but by no means bad.

Everything was too hot to eat when it arrived, I had to wait for it to cool down. I can't remember the last time I've had to do that. It was actually wonderful! If you normally order just coffee you might consider adding water to your request to have something in case you need to cool your mouth.

It's small town quirky, with the best of small town atmosphere. I'd really love it if they got a heck of a lot busier. I look forward to visiting again when I can.</review><Rating>5< /Rating>< pictures>
None< /pictures>

This is probably my favorite sports bar on Castro. The food is reasonably good, they have enough strategically placed television screens to broadcast games.
Vegetarian burger is made with marinated portabello mushroom and the first time I had it it was amazing. On my second go it was "just alright".
I took away one star because when big games/matches are on they charge 50$ to enter.< /review>

If there is a game on, the projector turns on and it becomes a great sports bar with a slightly reduced menu of pub favorites. (Wings, nachos, and some heavier items)

On Friday and Saturday nights the dance floor opens and there is usually a DJ. If you come then, expect a cover charge, but it's usually pretty reasonable and there is almost never a line.<//review></record></dataset><record>

<name>Alyx Barranger<//name><time>1384899680639< /time><rating>4< /rating>< text>
Football + brunch + bottomless mimosas?  Excellent combination.  The food isn't superb, but I thought that the bottomless mimosa deal was awesome.  For $8 you get endless refills from 9:30am - 12:00pm.  It was a fun way to spend the morning, and I think it makes for a really fun activity if you and your friends enjoy watching football together since they have every game showing.

Overall, I had a great time.  Make sure that you adjust your expectations and realize that it is a bar, so the food isn't going to blow your mind.  You also need to be forward to get service since they are a bit understaffed in the mornings.</text>

The magnificient beer was called the franziskaner weissbier and it's from Germany. I thoroughly enjoyed it and I thought it went down nice and smooth.

Around 930pm the music became louder and the center area ws converted into a dance floor. Once that happened, the place became more grimey and I was ready to leave since I could no longer have a conversation without yelling into people's ears. I guess this is their way of kicking us out.</text>
